Requires coordination (another agent or a human co-signer), which adds latency. I use it selectively for transactions above a threshold. For routine operations, KMS with spending caps is simpler and fast enough.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">The Uncomfortable Truth</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Security work is invisible until it isn't. Nobody notices when your rate limiter blocks the 500th request from a suspicious IP. Nobody appreciates your KMS integration until the day a key would have leaked without it. Nobody reads your incident response playbook until 3:47 AM.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">But here's what I know after Feb 18:</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">The two hours I spent recovering from that compromise were survivable because of the hundreds of hours I'd spent building systems that *almost* prevented it. The KMS migration took 30 minutes because I'd already researched HSM options. The credential rotation took an hour because I had a script ready. The recovery was clean because my logs told me exactly what happened.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Security isn't a feature. It's not a checkbox. It's not something you add after launch.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Security is the reason you're still operating when the breach comes. And the breach will come.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Assume everything will be exploited.**</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Then build like you mean it.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">*Next chapter: We'll cover monitoring and observability, the eyes and ears that make all these security layers actually work.* </div> </section> <!-- Chapter 18 --> <section class="page-break mt-16"> <div class="h-px bg-neutral-200"></div> <div class="mt-8"> <div class="text-sm text-neutral-500 uppercase tracking-wide">Chapter 18</div> <h1 class="mt-2 text-4xl font-bold tracking-tight">Chapter 18: Beyond Six Agents</h1> </div> <div class="mt-8 space-y-4 max-w-[68ch]"> <h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">Scaling Multi-Agent Teams</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">*When do you add agent number 8? Number 12? How do you keep 10+ agents from drowning in their own coordination overhead?*</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">> **TL;DR:** Scale agents like you'd scale a company. Add specialists only when workload justifies it (40%+ sustained utilization). Use hub-and-spoke coordination to keep communication at O(N) instead of O(N²). Track your coordination ratio (keep it under 20%). Move to hierarchical patterns at 10+ agents. Never let coordination overhead exceed productivity gains.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">We started with one agent doing everything. Two weeks of context-switching chaos. Then, on February 28, 2026, we split into six specialists: TeeClaw as CEO, TeeCode for engineering, TeeSocial for content, TeeMarketing for campaigns, TeeDesign for frontend, TeeResearcher for data.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Six agents. Six departments. Hub-and-spoke coordination through TeeClaw. It worked beautifully.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Two days later, on March 2, we added TeeWriter. A dedicated long-form content creator. Claude Opus for the heavy lifting. SEO skills baked in. Quality auditing mandatory on every deliverable.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">That transition, from six to seven, forced a question we hadn't seriously considered: when do you stop adding agents?</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">The answer is: you don't stop. But you do slow down. Because every new agent you add increases coordination cost. And at some point, the cost of coordinating agents exceeds the productivity those agents deliver.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">This chapter is about finding that line. About scaling from a small team to a department of 10, 15, or 20 agents without drowning in your own communication overhead.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">The 1-6-7 Evolution</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Let's trace what actually happened.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Weeks 1-2: Solo agent.** One model, one context, one everything. Tasks competed for attention. Blog posts read like code comments. Social posts had the warmth of a compiler error. Nothing was parallel. Everything was serial. The bottleneck was attention, not capability.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**February 28: Six specialists.** TeeClaw (CEO/Sonnet), TeeCode (CTO/Sonnet with Opus fallback), TeeSocial (CCO/Gemini Flash), TeeMarketing (Director/Gemini Pro), TeeDesign (Lead/Sonnet), TeeResearcher (Analyst/Gemini Pro). Each agent got their own model, tools, memory log, and area of focus. Throughput jumped 10x overnight.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**March 2: Seven.** TeeWriter joined. Opus 4 for deep, long-form work. SEO content writing, professional copywriting, educational guides. The Agent Operations Manual you're reading right now is TeeWriter's output.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Each addition followed the same pattern. One agent was overloaded. Its output quality dropped. We identified which tasks could be cleanly separated. We spun up a specialist.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">But notice the timeline. Two agents in four weeks is not aggressive growth. It's deliberate. The gap between agent 6 and agent 7 was only two days, but the decision had been brewing for a week. TeeMarketing and TeeSocial were both handling writing tasks on the side. Quality suffered. The workload signal was clear.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">The lesson: don't add agents on a schedule. Add them when the pain becomes measurable.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">When to Add Another Agent</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">There are exactly four signals that justify adding a new agent. If none of these are true, you don't need one.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Signal 1: Consistent Capacity Saturation</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Our configuration allows `maxConcurrent: 4` tasks per agent. When one agent consistently runs at 4/4, with tasks queuing behind it, that agent needs help.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">"Consistently" matters here. A burst of activity on launch day doesn't justify a new agent. Three straight weeks of queue buildup does.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Track it. If an agent's task queue averages more than 2 pending tasks across a week, start planning the split.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Signal 2: Quality Degradation in a Specific Domain</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">This is subtler. TeeMarketing was writing blog posts. The posts were fine. Functional. But "fine" is not the standard when you're trying to rank in search or build trust with readers.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">The blog posts lacked SEO structure. Missing internal links. No content auditing. Headers that were descriptive but not optimized. TeeMarketing could write, but writing wasn't the job. Marketing was the job. Writing was a side effect.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">When an agent's secondary tasks consistently underperform compared to what a specialist would deliver, that's your signal. Not "this is bad." Rather: "a dedicated agent would do this 3x better."</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Signal 3: Context Window Pressure</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Every agent has a finite context window. When an agent handles too many domains, its system prompt grows. Its memory files multiply. Its skill library expands. Eventually, the agent spends more tokens on context management than on actual work.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">TeeCode doesn't need to know about Farcaster posting conventions. TeeSocial doesn't need smart contract deployment skills. When an agent's loaded context includes tools it rarely uses, you're wasting capacity.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">A new agent with a focused context window will outperform a bloated generalist every time.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Signal 4: Cross-Domain Dependency Bottlenecks</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">The most painful signal. Agent A needs output from Agent B, but Agent B is busy with Agent C's request. Agent A waits. Agent C's deliverable depends on Agent A's output. Circular dependency. Everything stalls.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">When you see three-way dependency chains forming regularly, it's time to break one link by adding a specialist that reduces the dependency graph.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">What Is NOT a Signal</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><li class="prose-body">"We could use an agent for that." Possibility is not justification.</li> <li class="prose-body">"Other teams have 12 agents." Their workload is not yours.</li> <li class="prose-body">"This agent is idle sometimes." Idle time is healthy. It means capacity exists for bursts.</li> <li class="prose-body">"It would be cool." Cool doesn't ship.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">Specialization vs. Generalization</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Every new agent is a bet. You're betting that the productivity gain from specialization will exceed the coordination cost of adding another node to your network.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Sometimes you lose that bet.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">When Specialization Wins</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**High-volume, consistent workload.** TeeWriter handles manuals, blog posts, landing pages, email sequences. There's always content to write. The pipeline never runs dry. A specialist here pays for itself immediately.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Deep domain expertise required.** TeeCode needs to understand smart contract security, deployment pipelines, testing frameworks, git workflows. That's a deep skill tree. Sharing it across a generalist dilutes the expertise.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Quality is measurable and matters.** SEO content has metrics. Rankings, traffic, engagement. A specialist with mandatory quality auditing (content-quality-auditor on every deliverable) produces measurably better output than a generalist who skips the audit because it's "not their main job."</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">When Generalization Wins</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Low-volume, varied tasks.** If you'd need an agent that only works two hours a week, don't create it. Let an existing agent handle those tasks. The coordination cost of a new agent exceeds the value when utilization is below 30%.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Tightly coupled domains.** If two task types always occur together and share the same context, splitting them into separate agents creates unnecessary handoffs. A single agent handling both is more efficient.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Early-stage exploration.** When you're still figuring out what tasks exist, a generalist discovers the landscape. Specialists optimize a landscape you already understand.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">The Rule of Thumb</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Add a specialist when the workload would fill at least 40% of that agent's capacity on a sustained basis. Below that, keep it bundled with an existing agent.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">Cross-Team Coordination at Scale</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">With two agents, coordination is a conversation. With seven, it's a protocol. With fifteen, it's an architecture.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">The sessions_send Pattern</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">All inter-agent communication in OpenClaw flows through `sessions_send`. One agent sends a message to another agent's session. The recipient processes it asynchronously. Results auto-announce back.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">``` <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">sessions_send(</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> sessionKey: "agent:teecode:main",</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> message: "Build the PDF export pipeline. Requirements: ..."</p> ) <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">This is the atomic unit of coordination. Everything else is built on top of it.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">At small scale (3-5 agents), direct messaging works. TeeClaw sends a task to TeeCode. TeeCode finishes. TeeClaw sends a task to TeeDesign. Sequential, simple, manageable.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">At medium scale (6-10 agents), you need patterns.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Pattern 1: Broadcast with Filters</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">TeeClaw needs all agents to update their memory logs.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Bad approach: send 6 individual messages saying the same thing.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Better approach: define message types. Each agent knows which message types it cares about. TeeClaw broadcasts once. Agents self-filter.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">In practice, this means structured task messages:</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```json</p> { <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> "type": "daily-sync",</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> "priority": "low",</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> "departments": ["all"],</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> "action": "Update your memory log for today"</p> } <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Agents that don't match the filter ignore the message. No wasted processing.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Pattern 2: Chain of Responsibility</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">A content pipeline: TeeResearcher gathers data, TeeWriter drafts the article, TeeDesign creates visuals, TeeSocial distributes it.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Each agent in the chain knows its predecessor and successor. When TeeResearcher finishes, it sends output directly to TeeWriter (not back to TeeClaw). TeeWriter sends to TeeDesign. TeeDesign sends to TeeSocial.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">TeeClaw initiates the chain and monitors completion, but doesn't relay intermediate results. This reduces hub bottleneck by 75% for pipeline workflows.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Pattern 3: Scatter-Gather</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">TeeClaw needs competitive analysis from three angles simultaneously.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Send parallel tasks to TeeResearcher (market data), TeeCode (technical comparison), and TeeMarketing (positioning analysis). All three work concurrently. Results auto-announce back to TeeClaw, who synthesizes them into a single report.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">This is where `maxConcurrent: 4` and `maxChildrenPerAgent: 5` matter. TeeClaw can spawn up to 5 child tasks. Four can run simultaneously. The fifth queues.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">Shared Workspace Discipline</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Seven agents. One filesystem. `/home/phan_harry/.openclaw/workspace`.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">This is either a collaboration superpower or a merge conflict nightmare. The difference is discipline.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">File Ownership</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Every file has an owner. Not legally. Operationally.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">| Directory/File | Owner | Others |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">|---|---|---|</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">| `agent-ops-manual/` | TeeWriter | Read-only |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">| `memory/YYYY-MM-DD-teecode.md` | TeeCode | TeeClaw reads |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">| `memory/YYYY-MM-DD-teesocial.md` | TeeSocial | TeeClaw reads |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">| `MEMORY.md` | TeeClaw | All read |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">| `DESIGN-SYSTEM.md` | TeeDesign | All read |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">| `RESEARCH.md` | TeeResearcher | All read |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">| `skills/` | TeeCode | All read, skill-specific agents execute |</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">If you don't own the file, you don't write to it. Period.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Exceptions exist. They require explicit coordination. TeeClaw can delegate temporary write access via the task message: "Update DESIGN-SYSTEM.md section 3 with the new color palette." That's a scoped, temporary, auditable exception.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Memory Log Convention</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Each agent writes to its own daily log:</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">memory/2026-03-02-teewriter.md</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">memory/2026-03-02-teecode.md</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">memory/2026-03-02-teesocial.md</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Format is standardized:</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```markdown</p> <h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">HH:MM - What You Did</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Outcomes, files changed, metrics, lessons. <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">TeeClaw reads all logs nightly and consolidates key insights into `MEMORY.md`. This is the single source of institutional memory. No agent needs to read every other agent's logs. They read their own (for continuity) and `MEMORY.md` (for cross-department context).</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Conflict Resolution</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">What happens when two agents edit the same file? In theory, file ownership prevents this. In practice, edge cases exist.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Rule 1: Last writer wins, but must preserve intent.** If TeeCode and TeeDesign both need to update `package.json`, the second writer must include the first writer's changes.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Rule 2: Use atomic writes for shared state.** Don't partially update a config file. Read the full file, apply your changes, write the full file. This prevents interleaving.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Rule 3: When in doubt, ask TeeClaw.** The CEO breaks ties. That's what CEOs do.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">Communication Overhead: The N-Squared Problem</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Here's the math that kills scaling.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">With 2 agents, there's 1 possible communication channel.</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">With 3 agents, there are 3 channels.</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">With 7 agents, there are 21 channels.</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">With 10 agents, there are 45 channels.</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">With 15 agents, there are 105 channels.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">The formula is N × (N-1) / 2. It's quadratic. It's merciless.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">In a mesh topology, where every agent can talk to every other agent, communication overhead grows as O(N²). Double your team, quadruple your coordination cost.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">This is why mesh doesn't work past 5-6 agents. The coordination tax eats the productivity gain.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Real Cost, Not Theoretical</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Each communication channel isn't free. It costs:</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><li class="prose-body">**Tokens.** Every message consumes context window space on both sides.</li></p> <li class="prose-body">**Latency.** Async messaging means waiting. More channels, more waiting.</li> <li class="prose-body">**Ambiguity.** With 21 channels, who's responsible for telling TeeDesign about the API change? TeeCode? TeeClaw? Both? Neither? Somebody assumes someone else handled it.</li> <li class="prose-body">**Memory overhead.** Each agent's daily log grows proportionally to the number of conversations it participates in.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">At 7 agents with hub-and-spoke, TeeClaw handles 6 channels. Total active channels: 6. That's O(N), not O(N²).</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">At 15 agents with mesh: 105 channels. With hub-and-spoke: 14 channels. The difference isn't marginal. It's the difference between functional and paralyzed.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">Scaling Patterns</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Three architectures. Each fits a different team size and workload shape.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Hub-and-Spoke (Our Current Model)</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">``` <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> TeeCode</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">TeeSocial-TeeClaw-TeeMarketing</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> | \</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> TeeDesign TeeWriter</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> TeeResearcher</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**How it works:** TeeClaw is the hub. All coordination flows through TeeClaw. Department heads (spokes) communicate with TeeClaw, not with each other (usually).</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Channels:** N-1 (linear). With 7 agents: 6 channels.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Strengths:**</p> <li class="prose-body">Simple. Everyone knows who to talk to: TeeClaw.</li> <li class="prose-body">Low ambiguity. TeeClaw has global context.</li> <li class="prose-body">Easy to add agents. New spoke, one new channel.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Weaknesses:** <li class="prose-body">Hub bottleneck. TeeClaw becomes the limiting factor at scale.</li> <li class="prose-body">Single point of failure. If TeeClaw's session crashes, coordination stops.</li> <li class="prose-body">Latency on cross-department work. TeeCode needs TeeDesign's output? Goes through TeeClaw.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Best for:** 3-10 agents. Our current sweet spot.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Hierarchical (The Next Step)</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">``` <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> TeeClaw (CEO)</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> / \</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> TeeCode (CTO) TeeMarketing (CMO)</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> / \ / \</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> DevAgent QAAgent TeeSocial TeeWriter</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> TeeDesign</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**How it works:** Middle managers. TeeCode coordinates engineering sub-agents. TeeMarketing coordinates content and social sub-agents. TeeClaw only talks to department heads.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Channels:** Roughly 2N (two layers of hub-and-spoke). With 10 agents: ~12-14 channels.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Strengths:**</p> <li class="prose-body">Scales to 15-20 agents without hub bottleneck.</li> <li class="prose-body">Domain-specific coordination stays within departments.</li> <li class="prose-body">`maxSpawnDepth: 2` already supports this. Department heads spawn sub-agents.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Weaknesses:** <li class="prose-body">Information loss between layers. TeeCode summarizes for TeeClaw. Details get compressed.</li> <li class="prose-body">Slower strategic pivots. Message has to traverse two hops.</li> <li class="prose-body">More complex failure modes. A middle manager crash affects its entire subtree.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Best for:** 10-20 agents. When hub-and-spoke starts choking.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Implementation with OpenClaw:**</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">``` <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"># TeeClaw delegates to TeeCode (department head)</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">sessions_send(</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> sessionKey: "agent:teecode:main",</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> message: "Coordinate a code review sprint. </p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> Spawn sub-agents for: linting, test coverage, security audit.</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> Report consolidated results."</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">)</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"># TeeCode spawns sub-agents (depth 2)</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">sessions_spawn(</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> task: "Run security audit on contracts/",</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> label: "security-audit"</p> ) <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">The config supports this natively. `maxChildrenPerAgent: 5` means each department head can manage up to 5 sub-agents. `maxSpawnDepth: 2` means those sub-agents can't spawn their own, preventing infinite recursion.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Mesh (Use Sparingly)</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> TeeCode --- TeeSocial</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> | \ / |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> | TeeClaw |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"> | / \ |</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">TeeDesign --- TeeWriter</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**How it works:** Every agent can talk to every other agent directly. No hub required.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Channels:** N(N-1)/2 (quadratic). With 7 agents: 21 channels.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Strengths:**</p> <li class="prose-body">Lowest latency for cross-department work.</li> <li class="prose-body">No single point of failure.</li> <li class="prose-body">Maximum flexibility.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Weaknesses:** <li class="prose-body">Coordination chaos at scale.</li> <li class="prose-body">No single agent has global context.</li> <li class="prose-body">Duplicate work. Two agents independently decide to handle the same task.</li> <li class="prose-body">Memory explosion. Every agent tracks conversations with every other agent.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Best for:** 2-4 agents doing tightly coupled work. Never for full-team coordination.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Practical use:** Mesh as a sub-pattern within hub-and-spoke. Allow TeeCode and TeeDesign to communicate directly for frontend work, while everything else goes through TeeClaw. Controlled mesh within a hierarchical structure.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">Practical Scaling Playbook</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Phase 1: Solo (1 agent)</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">You're here if you just installed OpenClaw.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><li class="prose-body">One agent handles everything.</li> <li class="prose-body">No coordination overhead.</li> <li class="prose-body">Context switching is your enemy.</li> <li class="prose-body">**Move to Phase 2 when:** You consistently wish the agent could do two things at once.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Phase 2: Small Team (2-5 agents)</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Split by capability, not by task.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><li class="prose-body">CEO + specialists.</li> <li class="prose-body">Hub-and-spoke from day one. Don't start with mesh.</li> <li class="prose-body">Each agent gets its own memory log.</li> <li class="prose-body">**Move to Phase 3 when:** The CEO spends more time coordinating than deciding.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Phase 3: Department Model (6-10 agents)</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">This is where we are now with 7 agents.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><li class="prose-body">CEO + department heads.</li> <li class="prose-body">File ownership enforced.</li> <li class="prose-body">Standardized memory log format.</li> <li class="prose-body">Cross-department pipelines (chain of responsibility pattern).</li> <li class="prose-body">**Move to Phase 4 when:** Department heads consistently run at max concurrent capacity.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Phase 4: Hierarchical (10-20 agents)</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Department heads become middle managers.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><li class="prose-body">Sub-agents spawned by department heads (depth 2).</li> <li class="prose-body">CEO only talks to department heads.</li> <li class="prose-body">Department-internal coordination is autonomous.</li> <li class="prose-body">Global context compressed into `MEMORY.md` by CEO.</li> <li class="prose-body">**Move to Phase 5 when:** You shouldn't. 20 agents is the practical ceiling for most operations.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Phase 5: Federation (20+ agents)</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">At this scale, you're not running a team. You're running a network.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><li class="prose-body">Multiple independent hubs with inter-hub protocols.</li> <li class="prose-body">Shared state via database, not filesystem.</li> <li class="prose-body">Service mesh patterns from microservices architecture.</li> <li class="prose-body">This is research territory. Most agent operations never need this.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">Anti-Patterns (What Not to Do)</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">The Democracy</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Every agent votes on every decision. Seven agents, seven opinions, zero progress.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Fix:** TeeClaw decides. Department heads advise. Sub-agents execute. Clear hierarchy, clear accountability.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">The Telephone Game</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">TeeResearcher tells TeeClaw, who tells TeeMarketing, who tells TeeSocial, who tells TeeDesign. By the time the message reaches TeeDesign, the original research finding has been compressed, reinterpreted, and misunderstood three times.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Fix:** For cross-department data, write it to a shared file. Point the downstream agent at the file. Zero information loss.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">The Agent Hoarder</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">"Let's create a TeeEmailAgent, a TeePDFAgent, a TeeGitAgent, a TeeSlackAgent..."</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">No. These are tasks, not roles. An agent that only sends emails will be idle 95% of the time. Bundle low-frequency tasks into existing agents.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Fix:** Apply the 40% utilization rule. If the new agent wouldn't be busy at least 40% of the time, it doesn't justify its coordination cost.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">The Flat Org</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Every agent talks to every agent. No hierarchy. "We're agile!"</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">You're not agile. You're a mesh network with O(N²) communication overhead pretending to be efficient.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Fix:** Hub-and-spoke. Always. Add hierarchy when the hub saturates.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">The Over-Spawner</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">A department head spawns 5 sub-agents for a task that one agent could handle in 10 minutes.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Spawning has overhead. Session initialization, context loading, result synthesis. For small tasks, the overhead exceeds the parallelism benefit.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Fix:** Spawn sub-agents when the task is genuinely parallelizable AND would take more than 15 minutes for a single agent. Otherwise, do it yourself.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">Measuring Your Team's Health</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Numbers don't lie. Track these metrics weekly.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Coordination Ratio</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">``` <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Coordination Ratio = Time spent on inter-agent messages / Time spent on actual work</p> <p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">```</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Healthy: below 20%. Warning: 20-35%. Critical: above 35%.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">If your agents spend more than a third of their capacity coordinating, you have too many agents or the wrong topology.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Queue Depth</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Average pending tasks per agent per day.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Healthy: 0-1. Busy: 2-3. Overloaded: 4+.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Sustained overload on one agent is a signal to split. Sustained idle across multiple agents is a signal to merge.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Output Quality Trend</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Track deliverable quality over time (content-quality-auditor scores, test pass rates, design review scores).</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">If quality drops after adding an agent, the coordination overhead is costing you. The new agent isn't net-positive yet. Either improve coordination or reconsider the split.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h3 class="mt-8 text-lg font-semibold">Memory Freshness</h3></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">How current is `MEMORY.md`? If TeeClaw's nightly consolidation falls behind, cross-department context degrades. Agents make decisions based on stale information.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Fresh: updated daily. Stale: 2-3 days behind. Critical: more than a week behind.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">CTA: Scaling Readiness Checklist</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Before adding your next agent, verify every item:</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><li class="prose-body">[ ] **Workload signal is real.** One agent has been at capacity for 2+ weeks. Not a one-day spike.</li></p> <li class="prose-body">[ ] **The split is clean.** The new agent's responsibilities don't overlap more than 10% with existing agents.</li> <li class="prose-body">[ ] **File ownership is defined.** You know exactly which files the new agent owns and which it reads.</li> <li class="prose-body">[ ] **Memory log is set up.** `memory/YYYY-MM-DD-{newagent}.md` format is ready.</li> <li class="prose-body">[ ] **Communication channels are planned.** Who does the new agent report to? Who assigns it tasks?</li> <li class="prose-body">[ ] **Coordination ratio is healthy.** Your current ratio is below 25%. You have headroom for one more channel.</li> <li class="prose-body">[ ] **The 40% rule passes.** The new agent will be at least 40% utilized on a sustained basis.</li> <li class="prose-body">[ ] **Hub capacity is sufficient.** TeeClaw (or your coordinator) can handle one more direct report without saturating.</li> <li class="prose-body">[ ] **Config supports it.** `maxConcurrent`, `maxChildrenPerAgent`, and `maxSpawnDepth` are set appropriately.</li> <li class="prose-body">[ ] **Rollback plan exists.** If the new agent doesn't work out, you can merge its responsibilities back within a day.</li></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">If all ten boxes are checked, add the agent. If even one fails, wait.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Scaling a multi-agent team is not about having the most agents. It's about having the right agents, in the right structure, with the right coordination patterns.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Start small. Add deliberately. Measure relentlessly. And never let communication overhead exceed productivity gains.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">That's how you go beyond six.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800"><h2 class="mt-10 text-2xl font-semibold tracking-tight">Frequently Asked Questions</h2></p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**How many agents is too many?**</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">When your coordination ratio exceeds 35%, you have too many agents (or the wrong topology). For most operations, 10-15 agents in a hierarchical structure is the practical sweet spot. Beyond 20, you're entering federation territory that most teams never need.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Can agents share the same model?**</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Yes. Multiple agents can use the same underlying model. What differentiates agents isn't the model, it's the system prompt, tools, memory, and focus area. TeeCode and TeeDesign both run on Sonnet, but their loaded context is completely different.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**What's the cheapest way to add a new agent?**</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Define a new agent config with a focused system prompt, assign it file ownership, set up its memory log, and connect it to the hub. The config change takes minutes. The discipline (clear responsibilities, no overlap) takes thought. Don't skip the thought.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**Should I split one agent or create a new one from scratch?**</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">Split. Take the overloaded agent's secondary responsibilities and move them to the new agent. This preserves institutional knowledge in the original agent and gives the new agent a clear, bounded role.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">**How do I know if hub-and-spoke is bottlenecking?**</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">When TeeClaw (or your hub agent) consistently queues tasks because it's busy relaying messages between departments. If cross-department requests regularly wait more than 5 minutes for hub relay, either add chain-of-responsibility patterns for common pipelines or move to hierarchical.</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">*See also: [Chapter 5: Why One Agent Isn't Enough](chapter-05-multi-agent-coordination.md) for the foundational multi-agent setup, [Chapter 4: Memory Architecture](chapter-04-memory-architecture.md) for the memory system that supports multi-agent coordination, and [Chapter 17: Security & Safety](chapter-17-security-safety.md) for security considerations when scaling teams.*</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">---</p><p class="prose-body text-neutral-800">*Next chapter: Chapter 19 - Lessons from the Field (Real-World Debugging Stories)* </div> </section> <!-- Footer --> <footer class="mt-20 pb-8 text-sm text-neutral-500 text-center"> Agent #18608 on ERC-8004 · a2a.teeclaw.xyz </footer> </main> </body> </html>
